    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer263486252553830419"><b><i>Flat-Out Love</i> is a warm and witty novel of family love and dysfunction, deep heartache and raw vulnerability, with a bit of mystery and one whopping, knock-you-to-your-knees romance.</b><br/><br/><b>It's not what you know - or when you see - that matters. It's about a journey.</b><br/><br/>Something is seriously off in the Watkins home. And Julie Seagle, college freshman, small-town Ohio transplant, and</span>
  <span id="freeText263486252553830419" style="display:none"><b><i>Flat-Out Love</i> is a warm and witty novel of family love and dysfunction, deep heartache and raw vulnerability, with a bit of mystery and one whopping, knock-you-to-your-knees romance.</b><br /><br /><b>It's not what you know - or when you see - that matters. It's about a journey.</b><br /><br />Something is seriously off in the Watkins home. And Julie Seagle, college freshman, small-town Ohio transplant, and the newest resident of this Boston house, is determined to get to the bottom of it. When Julie's off-campus housing falls through, her mother's old college roommate, Erin Watkins, invites her to move in. The parents, Erin and Roger, are welcoming, but emotionally distant and academically driven to eccentric extremes. The middle child, Matt, is an MIT tech geek with a sweet side ... and the social skills of a spool of USB cable. The youngest, Celeste, is a frighteningly bright but freakishly fastidious 13-year-old who hauls around a life-sized cardboard cutout of her oldest brother almost everywhere she goes.<br /><br />And there's that oldest brother, Finn: funny, gorgeous, smart, sensitive, almost emotionally available. Geographically? Definitely unavailable. That's because Finn is traveling the world and surfacing only for random Facebook chats, e-mails, and status updates. Before long, through late-night exchanges of disembodied text, he begins to stir something tender and silly and maybe even a little bit sexy in Julie's suddenly lonesome soul.<br /><br />To Julie, the emotionally scrambled members of the Watkins family add up to something that ... well ... doesn't quite add up. Not until she forces a buried secret to the surface, eliciting a dramatic confrontation that threatens to tear the fragile Watkins family apart, does she get her answer.<br /><br /><i>Flat-Out Love comes complete with emails, Facebook status updates, and instant messages.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="263486252553830419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">No, if I have to answer in one word. No, if I explain it in more words as well but it's complicated. There's no love triangle but it might feel like t<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">No, if I have to answer in one word. No, if I explain it in more words as well but it's complicated. There's no love triangle but it might feel like there is one while you read the book. It's not possible to explain without giving away spoiler. But trust me when I say that this book has no love triangle.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

I think Jessica Park is a very talented author. She writes good. Or is it well? (That's why I'm a reviewer and not an author.)</span>

<div id="review_201330987" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/201330987" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/201330987?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781461085973" href="/book/show/12268263-flat-out-love">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Maja (The Nocturnal Library) by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/652877-flannery">Flannery</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=books-for-rainy-days">books-for-rainy-days</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=books-that-changed-me">books-that-changed-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=my-flat-army">my-flat-army</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=role-models">role-models</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=own-a-dtb">own-a-dtb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=self-published">self-published</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201330987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer194096707197714048">The first review I wrote consisted almost entirely of incoherent gushing. This one is pretty much like that, but I did manage to include some useful info. Don’t expect much, though. I can’t remember the last time I felt this way about a book. <br/><br/>As a dedicated reader, I don't think I've ever connected to a story quite this much. There are so many books that are close to my heart for some reason or other, but there was never one so achingly familiar and mine. And it wasn’t just one character that I </span>
  <span id="freeText194096707197714048" style="display:none">The first review I wrote consisted almost entirely of incoherent gushing. This one is pretty much like that, but I did manage to include some useful info. Don’t expect much, though. I can’t remember the last time I felt this way about a book. <br /><br />As a dedicated reader, I don't think I've ever connected to a story quite this much. There are so many books that are close to my heart for some reason or other, but there was never one so achingly familiar and mine. And it wasn’t just one character that I felt close to, but parts of every character and every situation. I recognized some of myself in Julie’s dedication to her studies, in Celeste’s quirks, in Matt’s courage and hidden vulnerability, in Erin’s absentness and denial. It was nice to be able to read a story and really understand. <br /><br />I’m making it sound like a sad book, aren’t I? Well, it’s not. This is a book you want to read when you're feeling a little nostalgic and disconnected from the world. It will pull you right out. Flat-Out Love is surprisingly witty. During the first 80%, I thought I could describe it as my favorite summer read. However, the last 20% showed me that it’s so much more than that. Every emotional reaction the story evoked was very strong: when I laughed, I laughed so loudly that I woke the neighbors; when I cried, I sobbed like I was facing the end of the world, and in the end, I melted into a huge puddle of goo. <br /><br />After moving to Boston to start attending college, Julie found herself living with her mother’s former best friend Erin and her seemingly perfect family of intellectuals. She soon became emotionally attached to every member of the Watkins family, especially the oldest brother Finn, whom she never met in person, but communicated with regularly via email. <br /><br /><i>”Happy families are all alike; every unhappy family is unhappy in its own way.”</i> (Leo Tolstoy) <br /><br />I think there are two types of dysfunctional families: the ones that yell and the ones that are quiet – the latter being so much harder to portray. Character development is what Jessica Park should really be proud of. Her characters came alive for me, they became living, breathing people with problems, quirks and a sense of humor. Who could resist Celeste, a scarily intelligent 13-year-old who won’t leave the house without Flat Finn, a cardboard cutout of her oldest brother? Or Matt, a math geek with horrible T-shirts and a sense of humor that’s right up my alley? <br /><br />Flat-Out Love completely changed my mind about self published books.I hope all of you will read it soon so we can gush about it together. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="194096707197714048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11096647-flat-out-love">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=my-kindle-challenges-me">my-kindle-challenges-me</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1256558593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4874764258731621392"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429295103i/14566469._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Congrats, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11096647.Flat_Out_Love__Flat_Out_Love___1_' title='Flat-Out Love (Flat-Out Love, #1) by Jessica Park' rel='nofollow noopener'>Flat-Out Love</a>. Welcome to the very limited circle of books I <i>hated</i>. Say hello to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15783307.The_Perfect_Game__The_Perfect_Game___1_' title='The Perfect Game (The Perfect Game, #1) by J. Sterling' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Perfect Game</a> for me, would you?</b> <br/><br/>Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1451367484' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kat</a> <i>(click to read her review)</i>, who saved my sanity (thanks for the support through this!!)<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452086382i/17644169._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>But because my inner circle of doom rewards its members as they deserve, let's start with little awards, 'kay? <br/><br/>But first of all........ <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QveJv7V4OZI' rel='nofollow noopener'>Music!</a><br/><br/>► It comes as no surprise that <b>Julie</b> easily earns the <b>most insufferable ès judgmental heroine medal</b> for her endless efforts </span>
  <span id="freeText4874764258731621392" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429295103i/14566469._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Congrats, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11096647.Flat_Out_Love__Flat_Out_Love___1_" title="Flat-Out Love (Flat-Out Love, #1) by Jessica Park" rel="nofollow noopener">Flat-Out Love</a>. Welcome to the very limited circle of books I <i>hated</i>. Say hello to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15783307.The_Perfect_Game__The_Perfect_Game___1_" title="The Perfect Game (The Perfect Game, #1) by J. Sterling" rel="nofollow noopener">The Perfect Game</a> for me, would you?</b> <br><br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1451367484" rel="nofollow noopener">Kat</a> <i>(click to read her review)</i>, who saved my sanity (thanks for the support through this!!)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452086382i/17644169._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But because my inner circle of doom rewards its members as they deserve, let's start with little awards, 'kay? <br><br>But first of all........ <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QveJv7V4OZI" rel="nofollow noopener">Music!</a><br><br>► It comes as no surprise that <b>Julie</b> easily earns the <b>most insufferable ès judgmental heroine medal</b> for her endless efforts throughout the story. The jury was really impressed by the abilities she showed in being a disrespectful and arrogant friend and daughter. <br><br>Here's a little presentation of her greatest deeds : Indeed through her constant inner monologues, we see <b>her unfailing perseverance in making fun of others</b>, whether she thinks they're dumb, lame, or annoying. Kudos for never forgetting that everyone and everything is beneath her. <br><br>✘ <u>About her former friends</u> : <i>"Now she was out of small-town Ohio, out of that below average high school, and out of a social circle dominated by girls blindly cheering on their sports boyfriends."</i><br><br>✘ <u>About her ex-boyfriend</u> : <i>"Speaking of Jared, Julie wondered what he was doing right now. Probably sporting a toga and doing keg stands at the miserable state university he was attending. She hoped he was lost in a crowd of dumb jocks and getting rejected by every busty, tank-top-wearing, fake-tanned airhead he hit on."</i><br><br>Wonderful. Just wonderful. <br><br>✘ <u>About random girls she doesn't even know</u> (but hey, she listened to their vocal messages, I'm sure it counts somewhere) : <i>"She didn't know if she was jealous of that fourth roommate or not. That Sally sounded an awful lot like the perky-yet-vacant crowd she'd left behind at home. On the other hand, there was something to be said about for a core gaggle of girls who would love nothing more than to order pizza, do each others' hair, and watch tawdry reality shows."</i><br><br>Wow. She got all these details out of the way the girl says hello on her vocal message? I'm really impressed.<br><br>✘ <u>Her conversations with Matt</u>, the son of the family welcoming her in their house, are full of "witty" bullying and aggressive remarks the poor guy never deserved. <br><br><i>"Let's discuss your choice of attire for the evening."<br>Matt hit the touchpad a few times. "Really? What aspects would you like to discuss?"<br>"Let's discuss how lame it is."</i><br><br><b>This is just fantastic, isn't it?</b> Don't you see how CLEVER and WITTY she is? What do you mean, you DON'T? Come on. Don't be like that. Not to mention that she does think about his life, too. Well, she doesn't want to invite him to come along when she goes out because, well, duh, he's so freaking beneath her (can you please follow?) but she considers keeping an eye on his sister someday to give him the occasion to attend a party. How's that for best roommate ever, huh? <br><br><i>"Not that he looked like the sort who was aching to do keg stands in a frat house, but still. There might be a physics bee some Friday night, and he could return home with a nice ribbon for having spelled "coulomb" or "neutralino" correctly"</i><br><br>Again, so freaking WITTY and CLEVER. <br><br>✘ <u>About her mother, in a text message</u> : <i>"Mom is OK. A little... lacking depth, maybe? But nice."</i><br><br>Don't worry though, because she really wants to help Celeste, the daughter of the house who is going through difficult times. Indeed she decides to take her under her wing, and manages to develop a bond between them without never making me care. That's an achievement to behold really. What can I say, I guess that <b>telling me that she cares isn't enough for me to believe her. Come on. We're talking about self-absorbed Julie here</b>. <br><br>See, I have no problem with unlikeable characters, <u>as soon as their behavior is acknowledged as being offensive</u>. <b>Never, at any point, is she called on her shit. Am I supposed to think that belittling everything and everyone is okay? That being plain bully with someone we just met is okay? That talking about a family welcoming you with your professor of psychology is okay? FUCK NO.</b> <br><br>To be honest, at one point Kat and I considered the possibility that Julie suffered from a mental-illness because the distortion between what we see and what she describes is freaking HUGE. Don't bother wondering, that's not the plot twist (more about that later). <br><br>► For the unrealistic and over-the-top quirky conversations, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11096647.Flat_Out_Love__Flat_Out_Love___1_" title="Flat-Out Love (Flat-Out Love, #1) by Jessica Park" rel="nofollow noopener">Flat-Out Love</a> wins the <b>award of the most unbelievable and fake set of characters</b>. Woohoo! <br><br>Look, I always considered myself as a nerd <i>but</i> by no means could I relate - or connect, at least - with any of these characters. Their interactions are ridiculous, roll-eyes worthy and more generally, completely unbelievable. Jessica Park's writing isn't bad, but she tries way too much to convey a sense of oddity. <b>Her characters aren't weird, they're freaking cyborgs</b>. <br><br>► Finally, for the predictable, "I-saw-it-coming-at-20%" plot "twist", I'd like to offer <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11096647.Flat_Out_Love__Flat_Out_Love___1_" title="Flat-Out Love (Flat-Out Love, #1) by Jessica Park" rel="nofollow noopener">Flat-Out Love</a> the <b>Golden Globe of easy roads</b>. I'm sorry, but when the big revelation is obvious from 20%, I consider myself insulted in my intelligence. <br><br>☻ ☻ ☻ Now, because I want to prove that I'm not one to hold a grudge, I prepared several little games about that *cough* ridiculous *cough* story. You're welcome. *blows kiss*<br><br><b>Find the words!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452040007i/17638123._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Complete the sentences!</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452086382i/17644170._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452086382i/17644171._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452086382i/17644172._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Cryptogram puzzle!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452086382i/17644173._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Answer : <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452086382i/17644174._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>

<div id="review_201184639" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/201184639" />
    <a title="Limonessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa"><img alt="Limonessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424025988p2/4147373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/201184639?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Limonessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Limonessa" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa">Limonessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11096647-flat-out-love">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201184639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5494303655921536189"><b>Have you ever...</b><br/><br/>-got a crush on a penfriend you never or barely met?<br/>-pined a whole year - or more - for your summer crush?<br/>-fallen in love with the <i>idea</i> of someone, idolizing him/her and thus making him/her perfect?<br/><br/>In other words: <br/><br/><b>Have you ever fallen in love with LOVE?</b><br/><br/>If you've recognized yourself in any of these questions, then this is the book for you.<br/><br/>Julie is from Ohio but she's starting college in Boston. When she arrives to find the apartment she thought she rented to be a total scam, her l</span>
  <span id="freeText5494303655921536189" style="display:none"><b>Have you ever...</b><br /><br />-got a crush on a penfriend you never or barely met?<br />-pined a whole year - or more - for your summer crush?<br />-fallen in love with the <i>idea</i> of someone, idolizing him/her and thus making him/her perfect?<br /><br />In other words: <br /><br /><b>Have you ever fallen in love with LOVE?</b><br /><br />If you've recognized yourself in any of these questions, then this is the book for you.<br /><br />Julie is from Ohio but she's starting college in Boston. When she arrives to find the apartment she thought she rented to be a total scam, her last resource is to call her mother's long lost college friend, Erin, to help her out and give her a temporary roof while she looks for a solution.<br />This is how Julie meets the Watkins family: Erin and Roger, the academic and self-involved parents, Finn, the fascinating older brother on a backpacking tour around the world, Matt, the middle brother, a math and physics nerd with a fetish for smartass T-shirts and Celeste, the 13 year old quirky sister of the family.<br />The Watkinses seem to be a regular enough family on the surface but Julie soon realizes that all is not well with these people's familial dynamics. What irks her the most is that she can't point her finger at the exact cause: everything seems to rotate around Celeste but there's <i>just</i> something that they are not telling her and that she is determined to find out...<br /><br /><br />This book would have normally received 4 stars from me.<br />If you're wondering to which genre it belongs, I'd categorize it as a more-adult-than-young YA college chick lit. And a very, very good one. Aside from being well written, it pushed all the right buttons for me.<br />It made me laugh out loud frequently, and not in a silly way but in a I-wish-I was-there-to-laugh-with-you way. <br />It took me back in time, wishing I could have back my late teenage years and the butterflies in the stomach feelings of my first crush(es). It really was a trip down memory lane for me. <br />It's got every good characterization and aside from Julie and Matt, I dare you not to be completely engrossed by Celeste and her personality. <br />Finally, it's got a very good plot and it's not very often that I can say that I was totally oblivious as to what would be missing piece of the jigsaw to understand the Watkins family.<br />I would have taken away a star, or maybe half a star, for the ending which I found excessively cheesy and slightly awkward.<br /><br />That is, if this book were a regular book. <br />But this book is self published. Now, my - somewhat limited - experience with self published books has been disastrous to put it mildly. Bad editing bothers me a whole lot. There are already many, many <i>published</i> books which are badly edited, I don't really see the point in subjecting myself to books which have not undergone the scrutiny of professional eyes and been polished. <br />But this is <b>NOT</b> and I was really and very pleasantly surprised. THIS is how it's done. For me, this book is close to perfect and if only for that it deserves the final missing star.<br /><br />Especially recommended for first crush nostalgics and hopeless romantics. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5494303655921536189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_326690436" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/326690436" />
    <a title="Nina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5109341-nina"><img alt="Nina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340635934p2/5109341.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/326690436?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina" href="/user/show/5109341-nina">Nina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11096647-flat-out-love">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5109341-nina?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer326690436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13615047649517924946">Ugh. Could not bring myself to finish this book. Julie, the main character, started to annoy me from Chapter 2 onward. But this got a lot of high ratings so I gave it a shot and soldiered on, but even after 100+ pages in, I still could not see why it's supposed to be good. Julie is the kind of person who will never be my friend if she existed in real life.<br/><br/>Almost each chapter began with a Facebook status of each of the three leads, but more often than not these didn't even have anything to do wit</span>
  <span id="freeText13615047649517924946" style="display:none">Ugh. Could not bring myself to finish this book. Julie, the main character, started to annoy me from Chapter 2 onward. But this got a lot of high ratings so I gave it a shot and soldiered on, but even after 100+ pages in, I still could not see why it's supposed to be good. Julie is the kind of person who will never be my friend if she existed in real life.<br /><br />Almost each chapter began with a Facebook status of each of the three leads, but more often than not these didn't even have anything to do with the story. And they weren't even witty!<br /><br />And the supposed "twist" was so easy to figure out, it shouldn't even be considered as such.<br /><br />I don't want to waste my time finishing this book anymore. I'm sure there are hundreds of other books out there more worthy of my time. Moving on.<br /><br /><br />UPDATE March 30, 2013<br /><br />I just found out that there is another version of this book written in the guy's point of view (Flat Out Matt). Why anyone would make another version of this insipid story is beyond me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13615047649517924946" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206998055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9238584513904567158"><b> Only .99 on Amazon 12/31/12, and if you haven't read it...it's definitely worth checking out!</b><br/><br/><b>5 HUGE STARS! Incredible book, from an incredible talent...I LOVED it!</b><br/><br/>Nothing flat about this book at all, it’s bursting at the seams with delightful characters, raw emotion, terrific dialogue, humor and heartache. This is a beautifully written unconventional love story. It’s hard to put into words how much this book touched me. Jessica Park is one of those extraordinary writers that draws you in and ha</span>
  <span id="freeText9238584513904567158" style="display:none"><b> Only .99 on Amazon 12/31/12, and if you haven't read it...it's definitely worth checking out!</b><br /><br /><b>5 HUGE STARS! Incredible book, from an incredible talent...I LOVED it!</b><br /><br />Nothing flat about this book at all, it’s bursting at the seams with delightful characters, raw emotion, terrific dialogue, humor and heartache. This is a beautifully written unconventional love story. It’s hard to put into words how much this book touched me. Jessica Park is one of those extraordinary writers that draws you in and has you feeling every emotion, good and bad. I wanted to stay with the Watkins and Julie forever, revel in their triumphs and help them to live, not just exist. I can’t recommend this book enough. It's a great read for teens and adults. Set aside time, because once you start you won’t be able to stop. <br /><br />Major spoiler!<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I knew the minute I met Flat Finn what was going on, but that detracted nothing from the story. You just keep hoping upon hope that what you know to be true...isn't. Then again my heart just broke for Matt, knowing that Finn's words were really his and if Finn existed, Matt would be heartbroken. You wanted to get to the point where all was revealed, yet I wanted to the book to go on so that I could stay with the Watkins, especially Celeste and Matt. Celeste will stay with me for a long time, I loved her as she was, through her transformation and healing. Matthew Watkins *sigh*, just an incredible human being! I can't even think about him without getting choked up. I wanted to crawl inside the book and wrap my arms around him and do for him what his own mother couldn't...give him comfort and love. In many ways I felt that he suffered the most, while everyone else lived in this fantasy world, he needed to hold it together in the real one. At times I had tears running down my face and when Matthew spoke the words "Finn is dead", I knew it was coming, but all the same it took my breath away. Julie always knew what the outcome would be, but in her own quest to be loved, she forged ahead with blinders on. The ending could not have been more perfect. Just thinking about it is bringing on another round of tears. This is a love story, love for a brother who’s gone, healing love, loving those left behind, loving oneself, and the beautiful love of two people who are so close, yet worlds apart. When they come together it will take your breath away! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer221807114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5955190017352556556"><b>*Update 06/12* My thoughts have changed about the book and my rating has been lowered. I am unable to explain why though, due to reasons which are not allowed to be stated because they are in conflict of GR policy of what is/is not allowed in a review.</b> <br/><br/><b>*Original Review for the book 10/11*</b><br/><br/><i>Flat-Out Love</i> definitely falls more on the "girly" side, but I enjoyed it almost as much as I enjoyed Anna and the French Kiss.<br/><br/>The story follows a girl named Julie who is swindled out of her money when she gets </span>
  <span id="freeText5955190017352556556" style="display:none"><b>*Update 06/12* My thoughts have changed about the book and my rating has been lowered. I am unable to explain why though, due to reasons which are not allowed to be stated because they are in conflict of GR policy of what is/is not allowed in a review.</b> <br /><br /><b>*Original Review for the book 10/11*</b><br /><br /><i>Flat-Out Love</i> definitely falls more on the "girly" side, but I enjoyed it almost as much as I enjoyed Anna and the French Kiss.<br /><br />The story follows a girl named Julie who is swindled out of her money when she gets to Boston and finds out that the college apartment she had reserved does not exist. An old friend of her mom's living nearby steps in and invites her to live with them - in the home of a completely dysfunctional family that is falling apart. Julie manages to take refuge in the emails and Facebook updates (some of which are completely funny) of the brother whose room she is staying in while he's off "traveling the globe." I don't blame her for falling for Finn, the human version of a cardboard cutout named "Flat Finn" that the little sister drags around because she's missing her brother. Then you have the complete math geek brother who can be a pain most of the time, but you can tell he's hurting inside as well because he shoulders a lot of responsibility for the family, which also makes you want to know more about him.<br /><br />I can not begin to explain this book well enough to do it justice. There was so much more to the story than I was expecting when I started. It always makes a book more special for me when an author can take the reader through a range of emotions, making you giddy and smiling one moment, and feeling the sting of hurt the next.<br /><br />Just by the name and summary, I figured that <i>Flat-Out Love</i> was going to be a light and potentially funny read, and it was. But there was a lot of heartache bubbling under the surface, which I hadn't planned on.<br /><br />If you're one of those people who feels like you've been reading the same story over and over, then you'll want to pick up this book. It's definitely different from anything else I'd recently read. <br /><br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_268103380" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/268103380" />
    <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog"><img alt="Aestas Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353371225p2/5604583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/268103380?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aestas Book Blog" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog">Aestas Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11096647-flat-out-love">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer268103380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7314643324136164481"><b> Wow! I absolutely FLAT-OUT <i> LOVED </i> this book!!!<br/><br/>"...that's what love does to you. Gut-wrenching, overpowering, crushing, fulfilling, complex, bring-you-to-your-knees love." </b><br/><br/>It was beautiful!! It kept me hooked right from the beginning. It was amazing, heart warming and a little heart wrenching, with light and funny moments, as well as deeply emotional ones. The dialogue was clever and witty and had me laughing out so many times. But this book was not a fluff read - it was deep, touching, and bit</span>
  <span id="freeText7314643324136164481" style="display:none"><b> Wow! I absolutely FLAT-OUT <i> LOVED </i> this book!!!<br /><br />"...that's what love does to you. Gut-wrenching, overpowering, crushing, fulfilling, complex, bring-you-to-your-knees love." </b><br /><br />It was beautiful!! It kept me hooked right from the beginning. It was amazing, heart warming and a little heart wrenching, with light and funny moments, as well as deeply emotional ones. The dialogue was clever and witty and had me laughing out so many times. But this book was not a fluff read - it was deep, touching, and bittersweet. Oh, and it has the best midnight drunken phone call ever! :)<br /><br /><i> "I'd just have to meet the right guy. Someone who isn't ordinary. Someone who gets me. Someone I fit perfectly with. I want heat, chemistry, an undeniable connection." </i><br /><br />Julie has a wonderful voice. The story had me smiling from the first few pages. It starts when Julie moves to a new city for college. The apartment that she rented off of Craigslist turned out to be a scam and she ends up staying with the family of an old friend of her mom's for the year. The family is kind and loving but Julie senses an undercurrent of something deeply wrong and hurt with them and she can't stop herself from wanting to help them heal even though she has no idea what is wrong. There is Matt, the hot yet nerdy brother who seems to take care of everyone, Celeste, the sweet and extremely bright 13 year old sister who carries around (everywhere),talks to and interacts with a life-size cardboard cutout of her eldest gorgeous brother Finn who is off traveling the world, to the absent yet loving parents who immerse themselves in their work. Julie is given Finn's room to stay in and she connects with him through Facebook and despite having never met him, feelings begin to develop for this charming, fun-loving and deeply caring guy that she just can't get out of her head.<br /><br />The characters in this book seemed so vivid. You really get the feeling when reading it that you are experiencing the story and its partly because of how much it integrates everything into the it - Facebook statuses, emails, private messages as well as the regular dialogue and story. It really helps to immerse you in the story and connect with the characters. You can very quickly garner so much from someone's Facebook status about their personality that just doesn't feel the same if you were told it. Most chapters start with each characters' Facebook statuses and through them, which helps you learn so much about them in a really cute and adorable way.<br /><br />"<b> Matthew Watkins </b> <i> I need an afternoon pick-me-up. I accept cash and/or prizes that can be exchanged for cash. Also, hobbits. </i><br /><b> Finn is God </b> <i> If you get off your high horse, you'll notice that it, too, poops. </i><br /><b> Julie Seagle </b> <i> Mixed emotions regarding Twitter continue. Am again facing warnings about unprotected Tweets, but it's not my fault the condom won't fit over the laptop. "A" for effort and whatnot, I think." </i><br /><br />This book is about relationships. Not just romantic ones, but also about deep family connections. It deals with many painful hurts that the family has experienced and throughout the book we see their healing process as this dysfunctional family puts the broken pieces of their lives back together.<br /><br />I loved how caring Matt was - how he was always looking after everyone, I loved how quirky yet so perceptive Celeste was, and I loved how flirty and understanding Finn was.<br /><br />This book made me misty-eyed several, it made my heart race and would often keep a smile on my face for pages on end. I totally felt sucked into Julie's world - into the affection she feels for Matt and his charming yet geeky personality, to the acceptance she shows Celeste and her strong desire not to give up on helping her heal, and to the growing attraction that she feels for Finn - as she slowly falls in love with him over their online communication. Honestly, I never thought I could fall in love with a character without actually 'meeting' them but boy was I wrong!! Finn had me falling in complete 'swoon' with him in no time.<br /><br />The writing is very fluid, the pacing is excellent - there are no slow points and no points where you feel like you missed a big chunk of time, Ms. Park's storytelling is addictive - I didn't want to put this books down. Given a choice, I would totally have read it in one sitting! <br /><br />There is a big family secret that leads to a twist to the end of the book! I had a gut-feelingin the beginning that turned out to be right and I'm curious to see how many of you also guess it :)<br /><br />The story has a wonderful HEA though - no worries!!<br /><br />I'd definitely call this book a must-read! I'd highly recommend it! And I think it's definitely a book that I will be re-reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7314643324136164481" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5495317-elizabeth-liz?shelf=ebook-read">ebook-read</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5495317-elizabeth-liz?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206527390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10577474093807978343">Goodreads asks me, 'What did you think?'. How in the world do I appropriately, adequately, answer that question with regard to Flat-Out Love by Jessica Park?! I'm certainly no author; I'm not even a 'real' reviewer. So, how do I put into words just how much I love this story and admire the talent and sheer genius of Jessica Park?<br/><br/>I don't do plot summaries, as should be more than evident by now. It's easy enough to read the summary and decide for yourself if this sounds like something that might i</span>
  <span id="freeText10577474093807978343" style="display:none">Goodreads asks me, 'What did you think?'. How in the world do I appropriately, adequately, answer that question with regard to Flat-Out Love by Jessica Park?! I'm certainly no author; I'm not even a 'real' reviewer. So, how do I put into words just how much I love this story and admire the talent and sheer genius of Jessica Park?<br /><br />I don't do plot summaries, as should be more than evident by now. It's easy enough to read the summary and decide for yourself if this sounds like something that might interest you. There's really no way I could do this plot justice anyway. I will say, briefly, that this story is about a family's pain and absolutely essential emotional growth. A young woman is introduced into this family, and becomes the catalyst for their re-emergence into the living world...painful as that may be. However, for all that this sounds like there could be no other option but for this story to be deep and dark and painful? It is just the opposite. It is intelligent, witty, strange, loving, dysfunctional, forgiving, accepting, understanding, and, ultimately, joyful. The characters are growing and becoming whole again, as you laugh and nod and think, 'No! Really?!'. Yes, really. Even if you, early on, guess the family's 'secret', as I did, you literally can. not. stop. reading. Jessica Park captures your attention from the beginning, and never lets it go, until the very end. And, by then, you're thinking, 'What?! It's over??'. We're advised so often to appreciate the journey. With this book, you do. You absolutely do.<br /><br />I cannot recommend this story highly enough. It is, without a doubt, a new favorite of mine, and, for me, an unequivocal 5-star read!!! Thoroughly unique and enjoyable! Do not miss this!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10577474093807978343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/320296880" />
    <a title=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida"><img alt=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295034921p2/1453659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/320296880?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" href="/user/show/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida"> Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11096647-flat-out-love">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">EVERYONE!</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to  Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~* by: </span>
      Karla
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer320296880" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer655594003056084070">(This is an Adult-who-enjoys-reliving-the-stirrings-of-first-love-and-self-discovery-during-the-teen-years-through-YA books review ^_^)<br/><br/><b>5 + Stars!</b> <br/><br/><i><b>Also reviewed at:</b> <a href='http://ladyjaynesreadingden.blogspot.com.au/2012/04/review-flat-out-love-by-jessice-park.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lady Jayne's Reading Den</a>  </i><br/><br/><b>WOW. I FLAT-OUT LOVE this book by self-published author, Jessica Park!!!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379771858i/302332.jpg' width='320' height='320' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This quote sums up how this book made me feel, how it inspired me through my journey with it, and even after I reluctantly closed its pages... <br/><br/>I’ve been struggling with my reading lately and I wanted a story that would really captivate me</span>
  <span id="freeText655594003056084070" style="display:none">(This is an Adult-who-enjoys-reliving-the-stirrings-of-first-love-and-self-discovery-during-the-teen-years-through-YA books review ^_^)<br><br><b>5 + Stars!</b> <br><br><i><b>Also reviewed at:</b> <a href="http://ladyjaynesreadingden.blogspot.com.au/2012/04/review-flat-out-love-by-jessice-park.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Lady Jayne's Reading Den</a>  </i><br><br><b>WOW. I FLAT-OUT LOVE this book by self-published author, Jessica Park!!!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379771858i/302332.jpg" width="320" height="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This quote sums up how this book made me feel, how it inspired me through my journey with it, and even after I reluctantly closed its pages... <br><br>I’ve been struggling with my reading lately and I wanted a story that would really captivate me and this is just what I asked for. Thank you to my dear Goodreads friend, Karla, for recommending this to me!<br><br>I haven’t written any reviews in a few months but I seriously just <i>HAD TO</i> write one to share my <i>LOVE</i> for this book! Please, give this book a go!<br><br>The story begins with this quote:<blockquote> <b>“It's not what you know - or when you see - that matters. It's about the journey.”</b>
</blockquote> This quote had me thinking from the get-go. <br><br><b>In Flat-Out Love, Jessica Park takes readers on an amazing journey with some incredibly crafted, quirky and lovable characters. This story is truly special because of the engaging, entertaining, sweet, heartbreaking and emotional journey it took me on. I was laughing, smiling, sighing, my heart aching, crying, and feeling positively giddy when I finished this. I hope it touches other readers as much as it did me. This was such a beautiful and wonderful story, with characters who will remain in my heart for a long, long time! Thank you, Jessica Park!</b><br><br>I loved it so much I bought the paperback.<br><br>Whether you’re a reader, like me, who feels you know what’s going on from the first few chapters yet keep hoping it’s not true, or a reader who is taken by surprise, at the end, one thing is for sure, even if you think you know what’s going on, I believe you will be captivated by this story, its characters, and staying up late to finish it. <br><br>Yes, there’s a mystery in this story, but this isn’t a Mystery book, and even if you figure out the secret early on, I don’t think it will detract from your enjoyment of the story. In fact, for me, having strong beliefs about what was going on with this dysfunctional family - even though I wasn't 100% sure - added a layer and subtext to my reading that had me feeling things I might not have felt, about certain communications, were it not for my beliefs surrounding the big secret of the Watkins family. If that makes sense… <br><br><i>Flat-Out Love</i> is an intelligent, unique, humorous, witty, quirky, warm and heartbreaking story of love, family, and coping mechanisms, but most of all, it is about a journey – several characters’ journeys – towards healing and living. <br><br>This is not a YA Romance per se, but there was certainly a beautiful romance in it. It is a slow-building romance, so please bear with it, because it had me in tears and smiling, at the end.<br><br><i>Flat-Out Love</i> is the story of Julie Seagle who moves from Ohio to Boston to attend college. I loved that this was a YA book set in the first year of college rather than the mostly high school fare out there. When Julie’s housing plans fall through, she is kindly welcomed into the Watkins home, the home of Julie’s mother’s college friend. But Julie discovers there is something “off” about this family, where their thirteen year old daughter, Celeste, has “Flat Finn”, a cardboard cut-out with her, for everything other than school, of her adventurous eldest brother, Finn, who is off travelling the world on various volunteer projects, and enjoys skydiving and bungee jumping.<br><br>I adored Julie and her clever wit, her ability to be so understanding of Celeste’s eccentricities, and her courage and strength to want to help the Watkins family. I also adored sweet, intelligent and nerdy Maths and Physics major, Matt, and how protective and so “there” he was for his family. I enjoyed Julie’s, Matt’s, and Finn’s Facebook status updates, Julie and Finn’s Facebook messages and chats, and Julie and Matt’s banter. And Celeste was just so precious.<br><br>It was humour like in this scene at the beginning, where Matt is picking Julie up, for the first time, which had me laughing out loud: <blockquote> <i>‘“Mom, I have to go. I think this Matt character is here."<br>"Are you sure it's him?" <br>Julie peered into the car as the window lowered. “I see a maniacal-looking guy with brightly-colored candy in one hand, and he’s waving a sickle with the other. Oh! He’s beckoning me to the car. This must be my ride.”’</i> </blockquote> And to share something of a scene that made me sigh and gave me tingles:<blockquote> <i>‘His hand was still on her back, his fingertips starting to trace the curve of her shoulder blade, moving up to brush the nape of her neck, then traveling up and down her arm. She took his free hand in hers, intertwining their fingers, and squeezed. <br>He squeezed back.’<br>…<br>‘His mouth was soft and unhurried. Teasing, even. His tongue brushing hers and making her tremble. She kissed back, tasting him, breathing him in. Julie was dizzy, and shaky, and inundated with his heat. He made her temporarily lost, not able to see beyond the way this kiss felt.’</i> </blockquote><br><b>HIGHLY RECOMMENDED!!!<br><br>My images of the characters…<br><br><b>Julie Seagle (Carly Rae Jepsen)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379773369i/317286.jpg" width="420" height="330" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Matthew Watkins (Benjamin Stone)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379773369i/317287.jpg" width="220" height="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379773369i/317288.jpg" width="430" height="330" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Finn Watkins (Alex Pettyfer)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379773369i/317289.jpg" width="420" height="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379773369i/317290.jpg" width="330" height="340" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Celeste Watkins (Chloe Grace Moretz)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379773369i/317291.jpg" width="280" height="370" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></b> <br></b><p>
  <br>
  <i>COPYRIGHT DISCLAIMER: I do not hold the copyright to any of the images used in this review. They are posted to add visuals to the review and for fun. If any of these images are yours and you would like me to remove them, please let me know, and I will do so as soon as possible. If I can identify the copyright, I will do so.</i>
</p></span>

<div id="review_327811164" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/327811164" />
    <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister"><img alt="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486056026p2/4971692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/327811164?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister">Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11096647-flat-out-love">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer327811164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16581154047239478750"><b>*5 Stars!*</b><br/><br/><i>Flat Out Love</i> was such a beautiful, touching, and heartfelt story that left me sorting out my feelings for days before I could properly sum them up. <br/><br/>I won't go into details over plot, as there is an extreme twist that I would hate to reveal, but I will say that I loved every little bit of this unique story! The characters were lovable and life-like, and I fully enjoyed their witty back-and-forth banter and charming dialogue. There were some moments, however, where I felt there could ha</span>
  <span id="freeText16581154047239478750" style="display:none"><b>*5 Stars!*</b><br><br><i>Flat Out Love</i> was such a beautiful, touching, and heartfelt story that left me sorting out my feelings for days before I could properly sum them up. <br><br>I won't go into details over plot, as there is an extreme twist that I would hate to reveal, but I will say that I loved every little bit of this unique story! The characters were lovable and life-like, and I fully enjoyed their witty back-and-forth banter and charming dialogue. There were some moments, however, where I felt there could have been a stronger distinction between some of the characters' personalities. Although each of them had their own unique quirks, their sense of humor and wit seemed to blend into one, at times. (I must add that this in no way hindered my love for this story.) Celeste, who is quite possibly the most unique character from any book I've ever read, was the major exception. I adored and rooted for her entirely.<br><br>I went into this book thinking I'd settled on a fun, sweet read — but was left with so, <b>SO</b> much more. This heartbreaking portrayal of a broken family brought me to tears, while an intense love strong enough to withstand it all amazed and inspired me. I was instantly sucked into this story and it has yet to let me go...<br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2mh7uop" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="50" width="50" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347313i/701667.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><b>
  <u>Book Stats:</u>

Life-like. <br><b>▪	 Plot:</b> Layered, original, with a twist in storyline. <br><b>▪ Writing:</b> Excellent. <div id="review_895693220" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/895693220" />
    <a title="BookLover" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12285159-booklover"><img alt="BookLover" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459818210p2/12285159.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/895693220?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BookLover" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BookLover" href="/user/show/12285159-booklover">BookLover</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11096647-flat-out-love">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=rs">rs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=author-first-reads">author-first-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer895693220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer480535648185995373">Full disclosure - I picked up this book a gazillion years ago and it got buried in my to-read pile. As is my style, I began reading it because of the pretty cover <b>WITHOUT</b> actually reading the description and reminding myself what it was going to be about. <br/><br/>This was such a unique story. Julie was off to college far away from home and excited to experience new things. She didn’t anticipate getting ripped off and having no place to live. Cue Erin, an old friend of her mother’s, who stepped in, via h</span>
  <span id="freeText480535648185995373" style="display:none">Full disclosure - I picked up this book a gazillion years ago and it got buried in my to-read pile. As is my style, I began reading it because of the pretty cover <b>WITHOUT</b> actually reading the description and reminding myself what it was going to be about. <br /><br />This was such a unique story. Julie was off to college far away from home and excited to experience new things. She didn’t anticipate getting ripped off and having no place to live. Cue Erin, an old friend of her mother’s, who stepped in, via her son Matt, to rescue Julie and gave her a roof over her head. <i>So at this point I was guessing this was going to be a romance about Julie and Matt, right? I was not prepared for the actual story-line and everything that was Flat Finn.</i><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“Oh, Julie! I didn't introduce you properly, did I?" Celeste chirped happily and then turned to the seat next to her. "Flat Finn, this is Julie. Julie, this is Flat Finn.”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />As a result of separation anxiety over her brother, Finn, traveling, Celeste had become un-naturally attached to a life-size cutout of her absent brother. For reasons Julie couldn’t pull from Erin, Roger or Matt, Celeste was enabled.<br /><br />In some ways, this had a very “Lars and the Real Girl” feel to it. (one of my all-time favourite movies- please don’t judge) Though very serious issues were at the heart of the story, I enjoyed the mostly light hearted approach to it, mainly thanks to Julie. I loved Julie’s outlook on life and, in particular, her no nonsense approach in trying to help Celeste come out of her shell. Her digs towards flat Finn were so dead-pan and hilarious.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>"He is a bit unsettled by this. I've never had my nails painted."<br />Julie turned around and glared at Flat Finn. "Every girl has a right to painted nails, so you better get settled quick, Flatty.”<br />“Celeste giggled. "Oh, he didn't like that name one bit."<br />"Tough.”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />In among all of the Celeste oddness, Matt seemed to have been left with the lion's share of responsibility in that household and I found myself so outraged on his behalf. I kept wanting to shake Erin and Roger and remind them both that <b>THEY</b> were the parents and Matt should get a chance to be a proper college student.<br /><br />Julie and Matt’s growing friendship was amusing and, though Julie seemed to be in the dark, it was super obvious to me that they had chemistry and a strong bond. The back and forth between them showed such a camaraderie and like mindedness.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“Bye, Matt. Maybe I'll text you in Webdings later and give you an update on my evening." Her heels clicked soundly on the floor as she headed down the stairs.<br />"Webdings one, two, or three?" Matt's voice rang through the stairwell.<br />"I'll mix and match!”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“What is this?"<br />"It's a gastronomical representation of 'Cat on a Hot Tin Roof.'" Julie put her hands on her hips. "Don't you see it? The clear depiction of the struggle for sexual identity as evidenced by the two phallic shapes?"<br />Matt looked at her. "What are you talking about?"<br />"What are you talking about? It's manicotti, you nut. What do you think it is?”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Even though I guessed the "twist" pretty early on I still felt like I had been sucker punched when the reveal happened. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I did not miss Erin constantly referring to things about Finn in the past tense. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Strangely though, I was more emotional for Julie than I was for anyone else impacted by it. I suppose that was largely because of all the lying that had taken place. <br /><br /><b>Surprising and delightful read!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="480535648185995373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=chick-lit-women-s-fiction">chick-lit-women-s-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer420179609" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15361368564955109920">**spoiler free review**<br/><br/>HOLY CRAP I LOVED THIS BOOK!<br/><br/>I did not expect for this book to so thoroughly blow my mind. Mind officially blown. <br/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380392108i/754948.jpg' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><br/>I feel like this review should be very witty because the book is so smartly written. It really took me by surprise. I've read so many insipid YA books that to read one that is written so carefully and so thoughtfully is like a shock to my system. <br/><br/>A quick plot summery: A girl (Julie) starts college in Boston but finds herself without a place to live, and ends up</span>
  <span id="freeText15361368564955109920" style="display:none">**spoiler free review**<br><br>HOLY CRAP I LOVED THIS BOOK!<br><br>I did not expect for this book to so thoroughly blow my mind. Mind officially blown. <br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380392108i/754948.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br>I feel like this review should be very witty because the book is so smartly written. It really took me by surprise. I've read so many insipid YA books that to read one that is written so carefully and so thoughtfully is like a shock to my system. <br><br>A quick plot summery: A girl (Julie) starts college in Boston but finds herself without a place to live, and ends up boarding with family friends of her mom whom she has never met. Still with me? The family consists of two absentee parents, both professors, a geeky brother (Matt) in his early 20s, an odd teenage sister (Celeste), and an even older brother (Finn) who has been traveling abroad for the past couple of years. <br><br>Celeste is socially awkward and, bizarrely, carries around a flat-lifesized cardboard cut out of Finn all the time. Julie ends up emailing and facebooking Finn to ask about Celeste's mental state and, over time, something more than online friendship ensues. But there are layers of mental health issues and entanglements that make their relationship increasingly complicated...<br><br>Oh how I love this book. I'm still dying over it and will probably babble to my husband the rest of the day about it. 2013 is so far a good book year!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15361368564955109920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
